\item 
using \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}{H\+R\+EF}} = \char`\"{}../../../c1\+\_\+element/bell\+\_\+element/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ the Bell triangular finite element$<$/\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../../c1\+\_\+element/curved\+\_\+element/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ the \textbackslash{}f\$ C$^\wedge$1 \textbackslash{}f\$-\/curved triangular finite element tutorials$<$/\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} $>$, for more detailed descriptions on the \textbackslash{}c Bell\+Element \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}c C1\+Curved\+Element.$<$ HR $>$$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a20230576f6747e2a6787209baaf0b8f9}{section}} overview Overview \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a thin shell \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} shell is defined \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a14facab9f61dcbec4928145e76337048}{as}} a thin three-\/dimensional elastic body where the thickness, \textbackslash{}f\$ h \textbackslash{}f\$, is smaller compared to the other two dimensions. Many analyses \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} thin shells neglect the effect \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the transverse shear \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} follow the theory \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} Kirchhoff-\/Love. This theory states that a normal \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a0a7df1853e74395dad518bf75eae1cad}{vector}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the undeformed mid-\/surface remains normal to the deformed mid-\/surface throughout the deformation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} it deforms inextensionally. Employing the Kirchhoff-\/Love assumption in a shell theory intends to reduce the dimension \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a shell \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a560411ef94f070ecd32898bd4df006cf}{problem}} from the three-\/dimensional to the two-\/dimensional theory. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, the shell governing equation which is derived from the \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7ef6f3c78549eab8eb95674c5a56e22b}{principle}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} virtual \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a32cfb7115626b7264ec3e48144b54015}{displacement}} can be reduced to two-\/dimensional space. This is a result \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} allowing the integration in the coordinate perpendicular to the mid-\/surface to be carried out analytically. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, all quantities can be expressed only on the two Lagrangian coordinates \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the mid-\/surface. Since the elastic material under consideration is a thin shell, the structure can experience large deflections \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} rotations, although strains \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} stresses may remain small. In such thin bodies, an assumption for small deformations(strains) is employed to simplify excessive deflections. This has been done by employing the linear(or Hookean) constitutive equation to represent the stress components \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a14facab9f61dcbec4928145e76337048}{as}} a linear function \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} all \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} components.$<$ HR $>$ \textbackslash{}subsection theory \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} thin-\/shell governing equation with a small \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} In \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a832530ba482d9170bb94c61a023f70f0}{this}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a20230576f6747e2a6787209baaf0b8f9}{section}}, we illustrate the linearisation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the governing equation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a static shell in a general geometry. It will be seen that a thin-\/elastic shell can be modelled by \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a6ad46d02702e84ec1d4dce2e585e38d7}{equations}} defined on a two-\/dimensional domain. To develop a mathematical description \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the deformation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a three-\/dimensional shell, we consider a shell geometry illustrated in the \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ac8ddc2c748c17fbaf4a008f7f83605d5}{following}} figure. From the thinness feature \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a shell, its geometry is allowed to specify by the two-\/dimensional reference surface \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} its thickness. We can choose the coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3=0 \textbackslash{}f\$ to be the shell \textquotesingle{}s mid-\/surface \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} the reference surface. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, we have that two coordinates \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_add7e4c9ab9db04ac3a0c51095555a89c}{xi\+\_\+1}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a743ff9dd1da9ed0c375ade197d65d1fb}{xi\+\_\+2}} \textbackslash{}f\$ are located on the reference surface where the third coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3 \textbackslash{}f\$ is normal to the reference surface. The upper \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} lower surfaces \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the shell have the coordinates \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3=h/2 \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3=-\/h/2 \textbackslash{}f\$, \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_aa2e2e9989ff9f7eaeffcda966d624ae0}{respectively}}, where \textbackslash{}f\$ h \textbackslash{}f\$ is the thickness \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the shell. @I w 0.\+45\textbackslash{}textwidth shell\+\_\+geometry \char`\"{}A shell geometry. \char`\"{} The \mbox{\Hypertarget{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}\label{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{HREF}{HREF}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}{H\+R\+EF}} =  \char`\"{}../../../c1\+\_\+element/bell\+\_\+element/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ the Bell triangular finite element$<$/\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}}$>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} $<$\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../../c1\+\_\+element/curved\+\_\+element/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ the \textbackslash{}f\$ C$^\wedge$1 \textbackslash{}f\$-\/curved triangular finite element tutorials$<$/\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}}$>$, for more detailed descriptions on the \textbackslash{}c Bell\+Element \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}c C1\+Curved\+Element. $<$HR$>$ $<$HR$>$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a20230576f6747e2a6787209baaf0b8f9}{section}} overview Overview \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a thin shell \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} shell is defined \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a14facab9f61dcbec4928145e76337048}{as}} a thin three-\/dimensional elastic body where the thickness, \textbackslash{}f\$ h \textbackslash{}f\$, is smaller compared to the other two dimensions. Many analyses \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} thin shells neglect the effect \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the transverse shear \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} follow the theory \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} Kirchhoff-\/Love. This theory states that a normal \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a0a7df1853e74395dad518bf75eae1cad}{vector}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the undeformed mid-\/surface remains normal to the deformed mid-\/surface throughout the deformation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} it deforms inextensionally. Employing the Kirchhoff-\/Love assumption in a shell theory intends to reduce the dimension \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a shell \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a560411ef94f070ecd32898bd4df006cf}{problem}} from the three-\/dimensional to the two-\/dimensional theory. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, the shell governing equation which is derived from the \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7ef6f3c78549eab8eb95674c5a56e22b}{principle}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} virtual \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a32cfb7115626b7264ec3e48144b54015}{displacement}} can be reduced to two-\/dimensional space. This is a result \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} allowing the integration in the coordinate perpendicular to the mid-\/surface to be carried out analytically. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, all quantities can be expressed only on the two Lagrangian coordinates \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the mid-\/surface. Since the elastic material under consideration is a thin shell, the structure can experience large deflections \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} rotations, although strains \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} stresses may remain small. In such thin bodies, an assumption for small deformations (strains) is employed to simplify excessive deflections. This has been done by employing the linear (or Hookean) constitutive equation to represent the stress components \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a14facab9f61dcbec4928145e76337048}{as}} a linear function \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} all \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} components. $<$HR$>$ \textbackslash{}subsection theory \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} thin-\/shell governing equation with a small \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} In \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a832530ba482d9170bb94c61a023f70f0}{this}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a20230576f6747e2a6787209baaf0b8f9}{section}}, we illustrate the linearisation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the governing equation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a static shell in a general geometry. It will be seen that a thin-\/elastic shell can be modelled by \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a6ad46d02702e84ec1d4dce2e585e38d7}{equations}} defined on a two-\/dimensional domain. To develop a mathematical description \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the deformation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a three-\/dimensional shell, we consider a shell geometry illustrated in the \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ac8ddc2c748c17fbaf4a008f7f83605d5}{following}} figure. From the thinness feature \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a shell, its geometry is allowed to specify by the two-\/dimensional reference surface \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} its thickness. We can choose the coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3 = 0 \textbackslash{}f\$ to be the shell\textquotesingle{}s mid-\/surface \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} the reference surface. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, we have that two coordinates \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_add7e4c9ab9db04ac3a0c51095555a89c}{xi\+\_\+1}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a743ff9dd1da9ed0c375ade197d65d1fb}{xi\+\_\+2}} \textbackslash{}f\$ are located on the reference surface where the third coordinate \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3 \textbackslash{}f\$ is normal to the reference surface. The upper \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} lower surfaces \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the shell have the coordinates \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3 = h/2 \textbackslash{}f\$ \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}xi\+\_\+3 = -\/h/2 \textbackslash{}f\$, \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_aa2e2e9989ff9f7eaeffcda966d624ae0}{respectively}}, where \textbackslash{}f\$ h \textbackslash{}f\$ is the thickness \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the shell. @I w 0.\+45\textbackslash{}textwidth shell\+\_\+geometry \char`\"{}A shell geometry. \char`\"{} The governing equation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a static shell with zero pre-\/stress is parametrised by the two coordinates \textbackslash{}f\$ This equation is presented with a non-\/dimensional form \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} is described in details in $<$\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a5d6485ed2a0c9b06578c585cef024399}{H\+R\+EF}}=\char`\"{}../../../beam/tensioned\+\_\+string/html/index.\+html\char`\"{}$>$ another tutorial$<$/\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}}$>$. Non-\/dimensionalisation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} quantities is also explained here. Note that in the small \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} regime, an area element between the undeformed \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} deformed configurations are indistinguishable. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8ec079733f9d91a62880f685ec37ee80}{Hence}}, the external force is preferable to express on the area element \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the undeformed midplane which is related with that \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the deformed midplane \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a14facab9f61dcbec4928145e76337048}{as}} \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\mbox{[} \textbackslash{}hat\{\textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_afc39b95cad3b7ff975f99b4d848ea063}{mathbf}}\{\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\}\}\textbackslash{}sqrt\{a\} = \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_afc39b95cad3b7ff975f99b4d848ea063}{mathbf}}\{\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\}\textbackslash{}sqrt\{\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}}\}, \textbackslash{}\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\mbox{]} where \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}bf\{\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\}, \textbackslash{}hat\{\textbackslash{}bf\{\mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a46a64ddd1219d813356c9849f14a0ccc}{f}}\}\} \textbackslash{}f\$ denote the external force expressed on the area element \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the undeformed \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9a91899e3790a7619f12a1802082d140}{and}} the deformed midplane, respectively. In order to obtain a linearised version \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} the governing equation \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a7f289c5bdbf801aa8460cb6057bb178e}{of}} a thin-\/shell deformation, all terms in the equation (@R\mbox{[}eqn\+:gov\mbox{]}@) have to be linearised. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a8250cb76c1bd25eeb3009b9fe8313010}{A}} small \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_ae205e3f5a4e48564cd4a106f6db67e82}{strain}} is then assumed. \mbox{\hyperlink{linear__shell_8txt_a9651a6ec028863df7c4ce6559109d167}{Therefore}}, we have that \textbackslash{}f\$ \textbackslash{}forall\textbackslash{}epsilon $<$$<$ 1 \textbackslash{}f\$,
